msg:The hotel is located in an alley in the ancient city of Chaozhou, which is quiet in the bustling city. It is more than 200 meters to walk to Paifang Street and Kaiyuan Temple, and more than 500 meters to walk to Guangji Bridge. It is very convenient to stay in the hotel and stroll around the ancient city. The hotel environment is elegant and the style of Chinese gardens. The facilities are relatively high-end, and the toiletries are provided by the Bulgari series, which is quite good.
The most important thing is that the hotel staff are enthusiastic and very patient! Ula and Leo warmly received us throughout the whole process and communicated on WeChat. The other staff I met were very kind and enthusiastic! The staff of Youxiong Bar and the buffet restaurant, as well as the shuttle bus driver, are very good. The hotel delivers fruits and desserts to the room every day. Snacks such as voss purified water and chocolate in the room are also free. The hotel rooms are not equipped with TVs, but there is free Chaozhou Yashixiang Dancong tea. You can experience Chaoshan Kung Fu tea in the room and yard in your spare time. In addition, next to the hotel is the former residence of Mr. Jao Tsung-i, and guests staying in the hotel can visit it for free.
This is the first time I have come into contact with the Youxiong brand under Vanke. I feel great for a two-day family stay. The hotel's environment, location, facilities, gifts and services are worth the room rate. A very good stay experience!

msg:I am a person who only likes to spend money and not write reviews, but after staying at Youxiong, I felt that I must write a review for this hotel.
1.Service
On the day of arrival, the front desk will proactively contact you to inform you of the parking space and provide a battery car to pick you up from the parking lot. For every trip during your stay, the hotel will provide a battery car to connect you to places in the ancient city where motor vehicles cannot travel. During my stay, every employee I met greeted me with a smile, took the initiative to say hello and provided proactive service. This is not easy. Nowadays, many five-star resort hotels priced at 2,000+/night cannot fully provide warm and friendly service.
2. Room facilities
The decoration is very Japanese, which can also be said to be modern and simple. The room is fully equipped with capsule coffee machine, teapot set, tea mineral water, Dyson blower, and bathroom facilities are all of high quality. The cloakroom is large and luggage can be placed very conveniently.
3. Quiet environment
Although the hotel is in the ancient city, it is very quiet and there is no noise at all in the morning.
4. Disadvantages
The lights in the bathroom are too dim, which is not friendly for women who need to put on makeup. It is recommended to install a retractable makeup mirror with a light.

Serve. Caring and thoughtful. We arrived at the hotel early and hadn't been able to check in yet. The lady at the front desk made us tea and the staff took us around Jao Tsung-i's former residence. Every staff member in the store will greet you when you meet them, and they are just right polite and warm. The lady at the front desk also informed you of weather, temperature, tourist attractions and other warm tips through WeChat. After 8 p.m., sugar water will be packed in thermos bottles and delivered to each room.
environment. The quiet courtyard is integrated with the modern space design. Walking in the courtyard feels very quiet, relaxing and very comfortable. The room was very big. It was so satisfying to drink tea with my best friends in the small courtyard, eat welcome fruits and play with mobile phones on the tatami.
facility. What surprised me most about the whole room was not the Dyson hair dryer or the shower room that is spacious enough for a family to take a bath, nor the Bvlgari toiletries, nor the smart toilet, nor the king size bed, but a small wooden bench in the dressing room. This little bench is so thoughtful when I‚Äôm putting on my shoes or packing my luggage! This has not been encountered in other star hotels. There is no TV in the room. I asked the lady at the front desk to help us install one if necessary. I was a little surprised that it could be installed temporarily. The service attitude was excellent.
breakfast. For a hotel in this price range, the breakfast is a little more refined, but I think it has everything it should have, including Chinese white porridge with preserved eggs and lean meat porridge, boiled eggs, rice dumplings, glutinous rice balls, rice cakes, vegetables, and freshly cooked rice noodles. , noodles, kuey gravy skin. Western-style bread, bacon, sausage, hash browns, and brewed cereal crunch. A variety of coffee, milk, soy milk, tea, yogurt, juice. fruit salad. Complete range.
health. Very clean, very clean, very clean.
Areas that can be improved: I saw butter in the breakfast area but not the butter knife. There was a coffee cup but no coffee spoon. The quality of pillows is average, not as good as Atour. Although the toiletries are from Bvlgari, they are not easy to use. The water is VOSS mineral water, but the cap is very difficult to unscrew. The sound insulation of the door is not good, I often hear people talking outside the door.

Having said that, I also want to talk about the problems seriously. I must declare: The problems mentioned below have nothing to do with any of the staff we have direct contact with this time. They are all great.

1. The butler service is very considerate, but lacks a proactive system to contact guests. If I hadn't taken the initiative to call the hotel, I wouldn't have known that the battery car could be picked up at the intersection before checking in. This would have caused great inconvenience and directly affected the first experience. Songtsan's system is in place on this point. As soon as you book a room, the housekeeper will take the initiative to call you and fully explain how to get there. Another note: We were not proactively notified of the excellent services such as battery-powered cars that can be used to tour some sections of the scenic area and tours of former residences. If we hadn‚Äôt read other guest guides and applied to the hotel ourselves, these services would be very difficult. May be missed;

2. The concept of Youxiong is to experience the city locally. We can clearly feel the bears in Shenzhen. This is why I took my parents to choose Youxiong in Chaozhou this time. Unfortunately, although the hardware brand, construction quality, and spatial scale of the room are all online, the design is lazy. It is difficult for you to feel the Chaozhou flavor in the room. It does not mean that crude placement of local customs or symbols is the sense of place. Of course, it can be designed to be restrained and subtle, and combined with a comfortable and modern experience, but it must be there. There is no room design this time. The so-called minimalism has really become simplicity, not simplicity. Afternoon tea is just a fruit plate, not even a local refreshment or a cup of local drink, and these are the strengths of Chaozhou that can be easily picked up! disappointing. Likewise, good night sugar water, mung bean soup and white fungus soup on two nights respectively. Ôºé †ïáThere is reason to suspect that the manager has not really understood and fallen in love with Chaozhou, even if she/he is a local. These are not a problem in ordinary business hotels, but they completely fall short of the concepts promoted by Youxiong.


3Ôºé The cloakroom and luggage room are large, but there are few hangers and no shoehorns. These themselves cost very little, but are useful and again reflect a lack of insight into the guest experience.

4. A hotel in this price range, without the hardware of a five-star hotel such as a swimming pool, should at least be equipped with bath salts and other bath products as a boutique high-standard hotel.

5. The refrigerator supplies are also too standardized, and none of them reflect local characteristics.

Having said so much, I still hope it will be better with bears, and I look forward to having the same surprise of first meeting again when we meet again in the next city!

msg:There are 20 guest rooms in Chaozhou Ancient City.
Vanke Youxiong Hotel is committed to the renovation of ancient buildings. The first family chose Jiayuan, the ancestral home of I.M. Pei in Suzhou, designed by Qingshan Zhouping. This time it was Chunyuan, the former residence of Jao Tsung-i. Li Yiliang hosted the event, and he was more precise in the local culture.
For example, the four points of gold, the octagonal gate, the Huoxiang, etc. were restored as before by Xiao Chuming, a non-hereditary person of wooden structure, and Ding Du, a famous ancient architect, and the lanterns at the entrance were made by Huang Qiuquan, another non-hereditary person. The interior design retains the openness and orderliness of Chaoshan mansions, using light wood instead of traditional dark paint, paired with handmade furniture by Tang Chunguang and selected books by Linghu Lei, incorporating the old into the new and interpreting the past with the present.
Nowadays, hotels are all about culture, but few are consistent in their words and deeds.
If there are bears, we are a family.

posted:Posted September 22, 2023
msg:There is a Bear Hotel in Chaozhou Ancient City owned by Vanke.
A lot of localized design, restoration and integration have been done, and the details are great. I borrow scenes from everywhere and see the big from the small. The service of every staff member is super good, butler-style service. I am very satisfied and will recommend it to my friends.
The former residence of Mr. Rao Tsung-i and the garden next to Youxiong were first built by Rao Tsung-i's father, Rao E.
Rao's father was a great scholar. He studied in Shanghai in his early years and often visited gardens in the south of the Yangtze River. After returning to his studies, he built a Suzhou Literary Garden style garden next to his house, and nicknamed himself "The Lay Gardener". The Tianxiao Tower in the garden was where the young Jao ‚Äã‚ÄãTsung-i studied, and the square pavilion in the garden was where Jao Tsung-i studied. A place overlooking the Han River.
In the 1950s, the former residence of Jao Tsung-I was transferred to Mr. Huang Jingyun, a friend of Mr. Jao Tsung-I and a cultural leader in Thailand. In 2011, the building was listed as a cultural relic protection unit in Chaozhou City and is now the Qiao Pi Museum.
